     修复「清掉进程后打开受限 app 不显示倒计时 widget」

     问题描述

     用户在「最近任务」中划掉本 app 后，打开被限制的 app：
     - 期望：右上角出现倒计时 widget
     - 实际：widget 没出现，但「禁用时段」的锁定提醒 overlay 正常弹出

     排查了  和关联文件，定位到 2 个独立但相互叠加的 bug：

     根因 A： 状态下 widget 被整体跳过

     复现路径：
     1. 上一次使用已触发强制休息（ 写入 DB，例如 10:05）
     2. 用户在休息期间（比如 10:03）在最近任务中划掉 app
     3. Flutter 引擎死亡，但前台服务仍在；DB 里的  保留
     4. 10:04 用户打开受限 app

     返回 inRest 会话

     7. 后续每 5 秒轮询都走 else 分支，widget 永远不出现

     问题描述

     用户在「最近任务」中划掉本 app 后，打开被限制的 app：
     - 期望：右上角出现倒计时 widget
     - 实际：widget 没出现，但「禁用时段」的锁定提醒 overlay 正常弹出

     根因分析

     排查了 lib/core/services/usage_monitor_service.dart 和关联文件，定位到 2
     个独立但相互叠加的 bug：

     根因 A：inRest 状态下 widget 被整体跳过

     _handleContinuousUsageTransition 行 152：
      final shouldTrackCurrent = !inRest && currentApp != null
      && monitoredApps.isMonitored(currentApp);
     只要 inRest == true，整个「显示 widget」分支就被短路——既不会创建
     session，也不会调用 _showStopwatchWidget()。

     isInRest 判定（continuous_session.dart:90-93）：
      bool get isInRest {
        if (restEndTime == null) return false;
        return restEndTime!.isAfter(DateTime.now());
      }
     复现路径：
     1. 上一次使用已触发强制休息（restEndTime 写入 DB，例如 10:05）
     2. 用户在休息期间（比如 10:03）在最近任务中划掉 app
     3. Flutter 引擎死亡，但前台服务仍在；DB 里的 restEndTime 保留
     4. 10:04 用户打开受限 app
     5. Flutter 引擎重建 → _syncAndCheck() → restoreSession()（不处理 inRest
     会话）→ checkRestEnded()（休息未结束，不操作）→ getActiveSession() 返回
     inRest 会话
     6. shouldTrackCurrent = false → _handleContinuousUsageTransition 进入
     else 分支 → 直接隐藏 widget
     7. 后续每 5 秒轮询都走 else 分支，widget 永远不出现

     根因 B：OverlayStateManager 重启后与原生侧状态失步

     _showStopwatchWidget() 行 199：
      if (await OverlayService.isOverlayShowing()) {
        return;
      }
     isOverlayShowing 查询原生 OverlayChannel.kt 的 isOverlayShowing
     标志，该标志在任何 overlay 显示时为 true。进程重启后 Flutter 侧
     OverlayStateManager._state = idle，但原生侧可能仍保留上次残留的
     overlay（兜底锁屏、time-block 弹窗等），导致 widget 永久无法显示。

     修复方案

     修复 1：inRest 期间也允许显示 widget

     文件: lib/core/services/usage_monitor_service.dart

     1. 去掉 _handleContinuousUsageTransition 中 shouldTrackCurrent 的 !inRest
     限制：
      // 修改前
      final shouldTrackCurrent = !inRest && currentApp != null
      && monitoredApps.isMonitored(currentApp);
      // 修改后
      final shouldTrackCurrent = currentApp != null
      && monitoredApps.isMonitored(currentApp);
     累加时间的逻辑（行 146 if (!inRest && _isSessionActive ...)）保留 !inRest
     守护，保证休息期间不累积使用时长。

     2. _showStopwatchWidget() 按 inRest 切换显示内容：

     - inRest == true → 显示「休息倒计时」（restEndTime -
     now），不设置锁定回调参数
     - inRest == false → 保持现有逻辑（显示 limitSeconds -
     session.totalDurationSeconds）

     修复 2：OverlayStateManager 初始化时与原生侧同步

     文件: lib/core/services/overlay_state_manager.dart

     新增 syncWithNative() 方法：清掉原生残留 overlay，重置状态为 idle。

     文件: lib/app/app_initializer.dart

     在 startMonitoring() 之前调用 await
     _ref.read(overlayStateManagerProvider).syncWithNative();

     修复 3：移除 _showStopwatchWidget 中过度保守的 isOverlayShowing 短路

     widget（右上角 TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY + FLAG_NOT_FOCUSABLE）与全屏
     overlay 在窗口层级不冲突。当前的 if (isOverlayShowing()) return; 只应防止
     widget 自身重复，不应因为别的 overlay 在显示就跳过。

     - 删除 _showStopwatchWidget() 行 199-202 的 isOverlayShowing 检查
     - 删除 _showCountdownFromRemaining() 行 241-244 的同类检查
     - 依靠 _countdownWidgetShowing || _stopwatchWidgetShowing 标志去重

     实施步骤
     ┌──────┬───────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────┐
     │ 步骤 │ 内容                              │ 文件                     │
     ├──────┼───────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────┤
     │ 1    │ _handleContinuousUsageTransition  │ usage_monitor_service.da │
     │      │ 去掉 shouldTrackCurrent 的        │ rt                       │
     │      │ !inRest 限制                      │                          │
     │ 2    │ _showStopwatchWidget 按 inRest    │ usage_monitor_service.da │
     │      │ 切换显示模式（rest                │ rt                       │
     │      │ 期间显示休息倒计时）              │                          │
     │ 3    │ 移除 _showStopwatchWidget 和      │ usage_monitor_service.da │
     │      │ _showCountdownFromRemaining 中    │ rt                       │
     │      │ isOverlayShowing 短路             │                          │
     │ 4    │ OverlayStateManager.syncWithNativ │ overlay_state_manager.da │
     │      │ e() 方法                          │ rt                       │
     │ 5    │ 冷启动时调用 syncWithNative()     │ app_initializer.dart     │
     │ 6    │ 构建并验证                        │ —                        │
     └──────┴───────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────┘
     关键文件

     - lib/core/services/usage_monitor_service.dart（中等修改）
     - lib/core/services/overlay_state_manager.dart（小修改）
     - lib/app/app_initializer.dart（小修改）

     验证方式

     1. 冷启动 + inRest：触发强制休息 → 在最近任务划掉 app → 重新打开受限 app
     → 确认 widget 出现并显示剩余休息倒计时
     2. 冷启动 + 非 inRest：正常使用中 → 划掉 app → 打开受限 app → 确认 widget
     在 5 秒内出现
     3. time-block 共存：禁用时段 → 打开受限 app → 确认锁定 overlay
     弹出，overlay 关闭后 widget 自动出现
     4. 原生兜底残留：倒计时进行中杀掉 Flutter 进程 → 重启 → 确认 widget
     正常显示，无残留 overlay 阻塞
     5. 累加正确性：rest 期间 widget 显示但
     _continuousUsageService.onAppStopped 不被调用（!inRest 守护）→ 确认
     totalDurationSeconds 不增长

 Thinking
 │ Now I'm refactoring the `_showStopwatchWidget` and
 │ `_showCountdownFromRemaining` methods to accept an `inRest` parameter, which
 │ will control whether they display the rest countdown or the usage countdown,
 │ and I'm removing the overlay check that was preventing these from running.
 │ The key insight is that during rest mode, I need to pull the remaining rest
 │ time from the service and display that countdown instead, with different
 │ lock parameters. I'm also removing the `isOverlayShowing` guards since the
 │ overlay and widget can coexist without blocking each other.
 │ Refactoring the method signatures... I'm handling the rest mode case where I
 │ fetch the remaining rest time, and if it's invalid I just return early. Then
 │ I'm calling the countdown display function with the appropriate parameters
 │ based on whether we're in rest mode or normal usage mode. For the non-rest
 │ path, I'm calculating remaining seconds from the session's total duration
 │ and the app's limit, then showing the countdown widget if there's time left.
 │ I'm also removing the overlay check since widgets and overlays don't
 │ conflict at the window level, and simplifying the countdown display function
 │ to always show from the remaining time without extra state checks.
 ▪ Step 2+3: refactor _showStopwatchWidget with inRest mode and remove

      208 +  ///                                                              
      209 +  /// 进程被划掉后 Flutter 引擎重启，OverlayStateManager 是新实例（
          +_state = idle），                                                  
      210 +  /// 但原生侧 OverlayChannel 的 isOverlayShowing 标志和残留 overla
          +y 可能仍在。                                                       
      211 +  /// 调用此方法清掉原生残留，让随后的监控轮询按规则重新决策弹窗。 
      212 +  Future<void> syncWithNative() async {                            
      213 +    try {                                                          
      214 +      if (await OverlayService.isOverlayShowing()) {

     修复「清掉进程后打开受限 app 不显示倒计时 widget」

     问题描述

     用户在「最近任务」中划掉本 app 后，打开被限制的 app：
     - 期望：右上角出现倒计时 widget
     - 实际：widget 没出现，但「禁用时段」的锁定提醒 overlay 正常弹出

     根因分析

     排查了  和关联文件，定位到 2 个独立但相互叠加的 bug：

     根因 A： 状态下 widget 被整体跳过

      行 152：

     A command-line utility for Dart development.

     Usage: dart <command|dart-file> [arguments]

     Global options:
     -v, --verbose               Show additional command output.
         --version               Print the Dart SDK version.
         --enable-analytics      Enable analytics.
         --disable-analytics     Disable analytics.
         --suppress-analytics    Disallow analytics for this dart * run
     without changing the analytics configuration.
     -h, --help                  Print this usage information.

     Available commands:

     Global
       install     Install or upgrade a Dart CLI tool for global use.
       installed   List globally installed Dart CLI tools.
       uninstall   Remove a globally installed Dart CLI tool.

     Project
       build       Build a Dart application including code assets.
       compile     Compile Dart to various formats.
       create      Create a new Dart project.
       pub         Work with packages.
       run         Run a Dart program from a file or a local package.
       test        Run tests for a project.

     Source code
       analyze     Analyze Dart code in a directory.
       doc         Generate API documentation for Dart projects.
       fix         Apply automated fixes to Dart source code.
       format      Idiomatically format Dart source code.

     Tools
       devtools    Open DevTools (optionally connecting to an existing
     application).
       info        Show diagnostic information about the installed tooling.

     Run "dart help " for more information about a command.
     See https://dart.dev/tools/dart-tool for detailed documentation.

     只要 ，整个「显示 widget」分支就被短路——既不会创建 session，也不会调用 。

      判定（）：

     A command-line utility for Dart development.

     Usage: dart <command|dart-file> [arguments]

     Global options:
     -v, --verbose               Show additional command output.
         --version               Print the Dart SDK version.
         --enable-analytics      Enable analytics.
         --disable-analytics     Disable analytics.
         --suppress-analytics    Disallow analytics for this dart * run
     without changing the analytics configuration.
     -h, --help                  Print this usage information.

     Available commands:

     Global
       install     Install or upgrade a Dart CLI tool for global use.
       installed   List globally installed Dart CLI tools.
       uninstall   Remove a globally installed Dart CLI tool.

     Project
       build       Build a Dart application including code assets.
       compile     Compile Dart to various formats.
       create      Create a new Dart project.
       pub         Work with packages.
       run         Run a Dart program from a file or a local package.
       test        Run tests for a project.

     Source code
       analyze     Analyze Dart code in a directory.
       doc         Generate API documentation for Dart projects.
       fix         Apply automated fixes to Dart source code.
       format      Idiomatically format Dart source code.

     Tools
       devtools    Open DevTools (optionally connecting to an existing
     application).
       info        Show diagnostic information about the installed tooling.

     Run "dart help " for more information about a command.
     See https://dart.dev/tools/dart-tool for detailed documentation.

     复现路径：
     1. 上一次使用已触发强制休息（ 写入 DB，例如 10:05）
     2. 用户在休息期间（比如 10:03）在最近任务中划掉 app
     3. Flutter 引擎死亡，但前台服务仍在；DB 里的  保留
     4. 10:04 用户打开受限 app
     5. Flutter 引擎重建 →  → （不处理 inRest 会话）→ （休息未结束，不操作）→
     返回 inRest 会话
     6. →  进入 else 分支 → 直接隐藏 widget
     7. 后续每 5 秒轮询都走 else 分支，widget 永远不出现

     根因 B：OverlayStateManager 重启后与原生侧状态失步

     问题描述

     用户在「最近任务」中划掉本 app 后，打开被限制的 app：
     - 期望：右上角出现倒计时 widget
     - 实际：widget 没出现，但「禁用时段」的锁定提醒 overlay 正常弹出

     根因分析

     排查了 lib/core/services/usage_monitor_service.dart 和关联文件，定位到 2
     个独立但相互叠加的 bug：

     根因 A：inRest 状态下 widget 被整体跳过

     _handleContinuousUsageTransition 行 152：
      final shouldTrackCurrent = !inRest && currentApp != null
      && monitoredApps.isMonitored(currentApp);
     只要 inRest == true，整个「显示 widget」分支就被短路——既不会创建
     session，也不会调用 _showStopwatchWidget()。

     isInRest 判定（continuous_session.dart:90-93）：
      bool get isInRest {
        if (restEndTime == null) return false;
        return restEndTime!.isAfter(DateTime.now());
      }
     复现路径：
     1. 上一次使用已触发强制休息（restEndTime 写入 DB，例如 10:05）
     2. 用户在休息期间（比如 10:03）在最近任务中划掉 app
     3. Flutter 引擎死亡，但前台服务仍在；DB 里的 restEndTime 保留
     4. 10:04 用户打开受限 app
     5. Flutter 引擎重建 → _syncAndCheck() → restoreSession()（不处理 inRest
     会话）→ checkRestEnded()（休息未结束，不操作）→ getActiveSession() 返回
     inRest 会话
     6. shouldTrackCurrent = false → _handleContinuousUsageTransition 进入
     else 分支 → 直接隐藏 widget
     7. 后续每 5 秒轮询都走 else 分支，widget 永远不出现

     根因 B：OverlayStateManager 重启后与原生侧状态失步

     _showStopwatchWidget() 行 199：
      if (await OverlayService.isOverlayShowing()) {
        return;
      }
     isOverlayShowing 查询原生 OverlayChannel.kt 的 isOverlayShowing
     标志，该标志在任何 overlay 显示时为 true。进程重启后 Flutter 侧
     OverlayStateManager._state = idle，但原生侧可能仍保留上次残留的
     overlay（兜底锁屏、time-block 弹窗等），导致 widget 永久无法显示。

     修复方案

     修复 1：inRest 期间也允许显示 widget

     文件: lib/core/services/usage_monitor_service.dart

     1. 去掉 _handleContinuousUsageTransition 中 shouldTrackCurrent 的 !inRest
     限制：
      // 修改前
      final shouldTrackCurrent = !inRest && currentApp != null
      && monitoredApps.isMonitored(currentApp);
      // 修改后
      final shouldTrackCurrent = currentApp != null
      && monitoredApps.isMonitored(currentApp);
     累加时间的逻辑（行 146 if (!inRest && _isSessionActive ...)）保留 !inRest
     守护，保证休息期间不累积使用时长。

     2. _showStopwatchWidget() 按 inRest 切换显示内容：

     - inRest == true → 显示「休息倒计时」（restEndTime -
     now），不设置锁定回调参数
     - inRest == false → 保持现有逻辑（显示 limitSeconds -
     session.totalDurationSeconds）

     修复 2：OverlayStateManager 初始化时与原生侧同步

     文件: lib/core/services/overlay_state_manager.dart

     新增 syncWithNative() 方法：清掉原生残留 overlay，重置状态为 idle。

     文件: lib/app/app_initializer.dart

     在 startMonitoring() 之前调用 await
     _ref.read(overlayStateManagerProvider).syncWithNative();

     修复 3：移除 _showStopwatchWidget 中过度保守的 isOverlayShowing 短路

     widget（右上角 TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY + FLAG_NOT_FOCUSABLE）与全屏
     overlay 在窗口层级不冲突。当前的 if (isOverlayShowing()) return; 只应防止
     widget 自身重复，不应因为别的 overlay 在显示就跳过。

     - 删除 _showStopwatchWidget() 行 199-202 的 isOverlayShowing 检查
     - 删除 _showCountdownFromRemaining() 行 241-244 的同类检查
     - 依靠 _countdownWidgetShowing || _stopwatchWidgetShowing 标志去重

     实施步骤
     ┌──────┬───────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────┐
     │ 步骤 │ 内容                              │ 文件                     │

     │ 1    │ _handleContinuousUsageTransition  │ usage_monitor_service.da │
     │      │ 去掉 shouldTrackCurrent 的        │ rt                       │

          位到 2 个独立但相互叠加的 bug：

          dApps.isMonitored(currentApp);

          ession，也不会调用 `_showStopwatchWidget()`。

 Thinking
 │ Now I'm refactoring the `_showStopwatchWidget` and
 │ `_showCountdownFromRemaining` methods to accept an `inRest` parameter, which
 │ will control whether they display the rest countdown or the usage countdown,
 │ and I'm removing the overlay check that was preventing these from running.
 │ The key insight is that during rest mode, I need to pull the remaining rest
 │ time from the service and display that countdown instead, with different
 │ lock parameters. I'm also removing the `isOverlayShowing` guards since the
 │ overlay and widget can coexist without blocking each other.
 │ Refactoring the method signatures... I'm handling the rest mode case where I
 │ fetch the remaining rest time, and if it's invalid I just return early. Then
 │ I'm calling the countdown display function with the appropriate parameters
 │ based on whether we're in rest mode or normal usage mode. For the non-rest
 │ path, I'm calculating remaining seconds from the session's total duration
 │ and the app's limit, then showing the countdown widget if there's time left.
 │ I'm also removing the overlay check since widgets and overlays don't
 │ conflict at the window level, and simplifying the countdown display function
 │ to always show from the remaining time without extra state checks.

      208 +  ///

      212 +  Future<void> syncWithNative() async {

 Thinking
 │ I'm realizing that `_diagNote` displays an overlay that auto-dismisses after
 │ 3 seconds, which could interfere with the widget display logic. When
 │ `_diagNote` calls `OverlayService.showOverlay` with reminder type, the
 │ native implementation hides any existing overlay first before showing the
 │ new one, so the reminder overlay gets displayed.
 │ Then when `showCountdownWidget` is called, it doesn't hide the reminder
 │ overlay—they stack on top of each other. Since both are
 │ TYPE_APPLICATION_OVERLAY, the widget should render on top if added after,
 │ but this is messy for debugging.
 │ For cleaner testing, I should either skip the success diagnostic or delay
 │ it, but for identifying which return path executes, keeping the diagnostic
 │ is worth the visual stacking since each path is tested independently. I'll
 │ rebuild and have the user test, and I should also add a diagnostic at the
 │ start of `_showStopwatchWidget` to confirm it's being called at all.
 │ Actually, there's a timing issue here—the diagnostic reminder auto-hides
 │ after 3 seconds, but if `_checkForbiddenApp` runs during that window and
 │ detects a time-block, it'll hide the diagnostic and show a lock overlay
 │ instead. Since lock has higher priority than reminder, the diagnostic gets
 │ dismissed and replaced with the lock screen, so the user won't see it.
 │ But that's okay—the diagnostic only needs to persist when no lock overlay
 │ appears, which is exactly when we need visibility into what's happening. Let
 │ me rebuild this.

   根因：两处 bug 叠加导致清进程后打开受限 app 时 widget 不显示——

   期间 widget 永远不出现）

 ▪ 需要了解具体现象才能继续排查。请回答几个问题：

 ▪ AskUserQuestion
   └ User answered:
       Q: 划掉进程后重新打开受限 app，现在看到的是什么现象？

 Thinking
 │ Now I'm narrowing down the issue — the widget isn't appearing at all, and
 │ the user was in normal usage mode when they killed the process, so this
 │ isn't related to the rest state. They can't provide logs right now, which
 │ limits my debugging options, but I'm starting to form a hypothesis about
 │ what's happening based on when the process was terminated.
 │ The most likely culprits are that the monitoring timer hasn't started yet or
 │ the foreground app detection is failing — if `currentApp` comes back as
 │ null, the widget won't display. It could also be that the user is in a
 │ forbidden time period and the overlay logic is preventing the widget from
 │ showing, or there's a session restoration issue where the old session gets
 │ deactivated but a new one isn't created properly when they open a restricted
 │ app. I'm also considering whether the `syncWithNative` call on cold start
 │ might be interfering with the initialization flow.
 │ Looking at the startup sequence in `app_initializer.dart`, permissions are
 │ checked, state is set, and then monitoring starts if permissions are granted
 │ — this should be fine since the MethodChannel is initialized first. The
 │ `startMonitoring()` function creates a periodic timer that fires immediately
 │ and then every 5 seconds, which should work. In the first `_syncAndCheck()`
 │ call, it handles day transitions, restores sessions, checks if rest has
 │ ended, and then tries to show the stopwatch widget — but if the active
 │ session is null, it clears the current app reference and deactivates the
 │ session flag before attempting to show the widget.
 │ When `_handleContinuousUsageTransition()` runs, it checks if the current app
 │ is monitored and calls `_showStopwatchWidget()` with `inRest: false`. This
 │ is where things could fail — if the settings aren't enabled, the foreground
 │ app can't be retrieved, the app isn't in the monitored list, there's no
 │ active session, or the remaining time is already zero, the widget won't
 │ display. Since the user was in normal usage before killing the process, the
 │ remaining time should be greater than zero, so if it's not showing, it's
 │ likely one of the earlier conditions is failing.
 │ For the first poll after cold start, `_lastPollTime` is null so
 │ `validElapsed` becomes zero, meaning no time gets accumulated. But the
 │ session gets created on that first `onAppStarted` call. When the user opens
 │ a restricted app and our app restarts fresh, the first `_syncAndCheck()`
 │ runs immediately — `currentApp` gets detected as the restricted app,
 │ `restoreSession()` finds the old session with its `lastActivityTime`
 │ potentially stale from before the kill, and if it's been more than five
 │ minutes inactive, the session gets deactivated.
 │ In `_handleContinuousUsageTransition`, since `shouldTrackCurrent` is true
 │ and `_currentSessionApp` is null from the deactivation, it triggers
 │ `onAppStarted()` to create a new session. Then `_showStopwatchWidget()` is
 │ called with `inRest: false`, which checks if the app is enabled, if it's in
 │ the monitored apps list, and retrieves the newly created session. The
 │ remaining seconds should calculate as the full limit since the fresh session
 │ has zero duration, so the widget should display.
 │ The fact that it's not showing suggests one of these checks is failing —
 │ either `getCurrentForegroundApp()` isn't detecting the app correctly, or the
 │ monitored apps provider isn't loading properly on cold start. So the
 │ `_showStopwatchWidget` function has several early return points where it
 │ could silently fail: if continuous usage settings aren't enabled, if the
 │ foreground app isn't being monitored, if there's no active session, or if
 │ remaining time is zero or negative. Each of these has a print statement, but
 │ without actual logs from the user, I can't tell which one is triggering. The
 │ key issue might be in step 4e where if the session is null after
 │ restoration, the widget creation gets skipped entirely.
 │ Looking at the session lifecycle, there are a few scenarios where no active
 │ session would exist: if the previous session was in rest mode and the rest
 │ period ended, `checkRestEnded()` deactivates it; if the session was inactive
 │ for over 5 minutes, `restoreSession()` deactivates it; or if there's simply
 │ no session from today. In all these cases, the code should fall back to
 │ creating a new session through `_handleContinuousUsageTransition`. But I'm
 │ wondering if there's a timing issue where the new session creation isn't
 │ actually happening, or if `getActiveSession()` is being called before the
 │ new session is fully persisted. So the real issue might be that
 │ `_showCountdownFromRemaining` is setting the flag and calling the native
 │ method, but something's failing silently on the Android side — maybe the
 │ overlay permission isn't actually granted, or the widget isn't rendering
 │ properly even though the method executes.
 │ Actually, I think I've found it: when the app gets killed from recents on
 │ certain ROMs like MIUI, the overlay permission can be revoked automatically,
 │ even if it was previously granted. So `hasPermission()` returns true, but
 │ the system still blocks the overlay from showing. That would explain why the
 │ widget never appears but the lock reminder does — they might be using
 │ different overlay mechanisms or the lock reminder is showing through a
 │ different path.
 │ The key difference is that the reminder overlay uses `MATCH_PARENT` with
 │ `FLAG_FULLSCREEN` and blocks touches, while the countdown widget uses
 │ `WRAP_CONTENT` with `FLAG_NOT_FOCUSABLE` and allows touches to pass through.
 │ Both are the same window type, so if permission is truly granted, both
 │ should work. But if the system is selectively blocking certain overlay
 │ configurations after a kill, that could cause this behavior.
 │ Let me think about whether the user is actually opening the companion app
 │ first or going straight to the restricted app after killing it — that
 │ distinction matters for when the monitoring service restarts.
 │ Actually, I think the real issue might be in the `_syncAndCheck` flow
 │ itself. When the foreground app changes, it triggers `_checkTimeBlockRule`,
 │ which either shows a reminder overlay if the app is blocked, or calls
 │ `hideReminder()` to dismiss it. That `dismissCurrent()` method acquires a
 │ lock and hides the overlay through the native service. But here's the thing:
 │ if the overlay state transitions to idle while the reminder is being hidden,
 │ and then `_showStopwatchWidget` tries to show the countdown widget, there
 │ could be a race condition where the overlay is being torn down at the same
 │ time the widget is being created.
 │ Let me add some diagnostic logging to trace exactly what's happening when

 │ certain conditions are met.
 │ Actually, let me reconsider what the user said about clearing the process
 │ from recents. When an app is cleared from recent tasks on Android, the task
 │ is removed, all activities are destroyed, and services with `START_STICKY`
 │ get restarted by the system. If our `MonitorForegroundService` uses
 │ `START_STICKY`, then after clearing from recents, the system would restart
 │ the service, which would trigger `startNativeMonitoring()` and check
 │ `AppLockManager.shouldShowLock()` to display the lock overlay if needed.

 │ recents, `MainActivity` is created fresh, which triggers the initialization
 │ sequence including `syncWithNative()` and `startMonitoring()`. This calls
 │ `_syncAndCheck()` immediately, which reads the foreground app via
 │ `UsageStatsService` through a MethodChannel. The issue might be that
 │ `UsageStatsHelper.getCurrentForegroundApp()` is returning `null` due to a
 │ race condition where `UsageStatsManager` hasn't yet recorded the restricted
 │ app as foreground.

 │ detection is working. The key difference is that `_lastForegroundApp`
 │ persists from the previous session, so on the first poll after clearing
 │ recents, it's `null` (no reminder shown), but on the second poll 5 seconds
 │ later, it's set to the restricted app (reminder shown). This suggests the
 │ widget should also appear on the second poll if all conditions are met, but
 │ it's not. Let me trace through the exact sequence of the second poll to find
 │ where the widget logic breaks down. I'm realizing the widget and overlay are
 │ managed separately—the native side hides the old overlay when showing a new
 │ one, but the widget persists. The real issue might be a race condition: when
 │ the time block overlay is requested in step 7, it goes through the state
 │ manager's lock and shows via the MethodChannel. Then in step 10, the
 │ reminder service checks if it's a hard limit and calls `isOverlayActive()`,
 │ which checks both the state and the native side—but by this point the
 │ overlay is already showing, so it might be trying to show it again or
 │ there's a timing issue with the lock release.

   期间 widget 永远不出现）

   isOverlayShowing 保守短路

 Thinking
 │ I'm realizing the core issue: when the app process gets killed from recent
 │ tasks, the Flutter engine stops running, but the native
 │ `MonitorForegroundService` keeps going with its monitoring loop checking the
 │ foreground app every 5 seconds. The problem is that when Flutter is dead,
 │ only the countdown recovery runs — the usage monitoring logic that should
 │ trigger when a restricted app opens doesn't execute because it depends on
 │ the Flutter side being alive.
 │ The native layer does have a blocking mechanism that checks time periods and
 │ total usage limits through `NativeRuleChecker.checkApp()`, but it's missing
 │ a critical feature: there's no native countdown widget like the Flutter side
 │ has. The native side only displays lock screens when access is blocked, or
 │ restores an existing countdown if one was already running — but it can't
 │ create a new countdown widget from scratch. So if no lock condition is
 │ triggered, nothing appears on screen at all.
 │ There's also a deeper issue with the Flutter engine itself. When the user
 │ opens a restricted app after killing the process, nothing wakes up the
 │ Flutter engine — the native side detects the app but doesn't launch
 │ MainActivity to restart it. Without the Flutter engine running, the usage
 │ monitoring service and all its checks never execute, so the widget can't be
 │ created.
 │ The solution requires two parts: first, when the native side detects a
 │ monitored app and Flutter is dead, it needs to wake up the Flutter engine
 │ through either a transparent MainActivity or a background engine
 │ initialization; second, the native layer needs to be able to display a
 │ countdown widget independently, not just lock screens, so it can show the
 │ timer even when no blocking rule is triggered.
 │ The most direct approach is having the native side start MainActivity when
 │ it detects a monitored app while Flutter is dead. Since MainActivity uses
 │ `singleTop` launch mode, it'll trigger `onNewIntent` if already running or
 │ `onCreate` if not, which will initialize the Flutter engine and start
 │ monitoring. This should happen immediately when the monitored app comes to
 │ the foreground, with minimal visual disruption since MainActivity would
 │ appear briefly before the user returns to their app.
 │ But I need to verify a few things first: what exactly does
 │ `NativeRuleChecker` classify as a "monitored app"? Does it only flag
 │ time-block violations, or does it also recognize apps that should have the
 │ countdown widget? And is there actually a native-side list of monitored apps
 │ I can reference? Let me check how `NativeRuleChecker` is structured to
 │ understand what data I'm working with.

 │ I see that `NativeRuleChecker.checkApp()` gives me what I need—it returns

 │ solution is to proactively restart MainActivity on the first detection of a

 ▪ 定位到根因：划掉进程后 Flutter 引擎没被重建。原生 MonitorForegroundService

 Thinking
 │ I'm realizing the core issue: when the app process gets killed from recent
 │ tasks, the Flutter engine stops running, but the native
 │ `MonitorForegroundService` keeps going with its monitoring loop checking the
 │ foreground app every 5 seconds. The problem is that when Flutter is dead,
 │ only the countdown recovery runs — the usage monitoring logic that should
 │ trigger when a restricted app opens doesn't execute because it depends on
 │ the Flutter side being alive.
 │ The native layer does have a blocking mechanism that checks time periods and
 │ total usage limits through `NativeRuleChecker.checkApp()`, but it's missing
 │ a critical feature: there's no native countdown widget like the Flutter side
 │ has. The native side only displays lock screens when access is blocked, or
 │ restores an existing countdown if one was already running — but it can't
 │ create a new countdown widget from scratch. So if no lock condition is
 │ triggered, nothing appears on screen at all.
 │ There's also a deeper issue with the Flutter engine itself. When the user
 │ opens a restricted app after killing the process, nothing wakes up the
 │ Flutter engine — the native side detects the app but doesn't launch
 │ MainActivity to restart it. Without the Flutter engine running, the usage
 │ monitoring service and all its checks never execute, so the widget can't be
 │ created.
 │ The solution requires two parts: first, when the native side detects a
 │ monitored app and Flutter is dead, it needs to wake up the Flutter engine
 │ through either a transparent MainActivity or a background engine
 │ initialization; second, the native layer needs to be able to display a
 │ countdown widget independently, not just lock screens, so it can show the
 │ timer even when no blocking rule is triggered.
 │ The most direct approach is having the native side start MainActivity when
 │ it detects a monitored app while Flutter is dead. Since MainActivity uses
 │ `singleTop` launch mode, it'll trigger `onNewIntent` if already running or
 │ `onCreate` if not, which will initialize the Flutter engine and start
 │ monitoring. This should happen immediately when the monitored app comes to
 │ the foreground, with minimal visual disruption since MainActivity would
 │ appear briefly before the user returns to their app.
 │ But I need to verify a few things first: what exactly does
 │ `NativeRuleChecker` classify as a "monitored app"? Does it only flag
 │ time-block violations, or does it also recognize apps that should have the
 │ countdown widget? And is there actually a native-side list of monitored apps
 │ I can reference? Let me check how `NativeRuleChecker` is structured to
 │ understand what data I'm working with.

 │ I see that `NativeRuleChecker.checkApp()` gives me what I need—it returns

 │ would be cleaner but requires adding a new Activity and manifest entry.
 │ Looking at this more carefully, the real issue is that the user wants the
 │ countdown widget to appear after the app is killed, which means Flutter
 │ needs to restart and calculate the remaining time. The most pragmatic
 │ solution is to proactively restart MainActivity on the first detection of a
 │ monitored app, using the `FLAG_ACTIVITY_NEW_TASK` flag to launch it without
 │ disrupting the current task stack too much. I'll modify
 │ `MonitorForegroundService.monitorRunnable` step B to check if the app is
 │ monitored but not blocked, and if so, start MainActivity with an action like
 │ "WAKEUP" to trigger the Flutter engine initialization.
 │ To avoid repeatedly restarting MainActivity, I should add a flag in the
 │ service to track whether we've already triggered a wake-up in this cycle,
 │ and reset it when Flutter comes back alive. Then in

 │ immediately, so the user stays on their restricted app while Flutter runs in
 │ the background and shows the widget.
 │ Alternatively, I could use a headless Flutter engine that runs without any
 │ UI at all, but that's more complex. The simpler approach is to just start
 │ MainActivity with the WAKEUP action and have it immediately background

 ▪ 定位到根因：划掉进程后 Flutter 引擎没被重建。原生 MonitorForegroundService
   一直在跑（所以时间块锁能弹），但检测到受监控 app 时不会主动拉起 Flutter
   引擎，导致 Dart 侧的 _showStopwatchWidget 和所有诊断都执行不到。

   唤醒引擎，然后立即 moveTaskToBack 把界面藏起来。

 Thinking
 │ I'm realizing the core issue: when the app process gets killed from recent
 │ tasks, the Flutter engine stops running, but the native
 │ `MonitorForegroundService` keeps going with its monitoring loop checking the
 │ foreground app every 5 seconds. The problem is that when Flutter is dead,
 │ only the countdown recovery runs — the usage monitoring logic that should
 │ trigger when a restricted app opens doesn't execute because it depends on
 │ the Flutter side being alive.
 │ The native layer does have a blocking mechanism that checks time periods and
 │ total usage limits through `NativeRuleChecker.checkApp()`, but it's missing
 │ a critical feature: there's no native countdown widget like the Flutter side
 │ has. The native side only displays lock screens when access is blocked, or
 │ restores an existing countdown if one was already running — but it can't
 │ create a new countdown widget from scratch. So if no lock condition is
 │ triggered, nothing appears on screen at all.
 │ There's also a deeper issue with the Flutter engine itself. When the user
 │ opens a restricted app after killing the process, nothing wakes up the
 │ Flutter engine — the native side detects the app but doesn't launch
 │ MainActivity to restart it. Without the Flutter engine running, the usage
 │ monitoring service and all its checks never execute, so the widget can't be
 │ created.
 │ The solution requires two parts: first, when the native side detects a
 │ monitored app and Flutter is dead, it needs to wake up the Flutter engine
 │ through either a transparent MainActivity or a background engine
 │ initialization; second, the native layer needs to be able to display a
 │ countdown widget independently, not just lock screens, so it can show the
 │ timer even when no blocking rule is triggered.
 │ The most direct approach is having the native side start MainActivity when
 │ it detects a monitored app while Flutter is dead. Since MainActivity uses
 │ `singleTop` launch mode, it'll trigger `onNewIntent` if already running or
 │ `onCreate` if not, which will initialize the Flutter engine and start
 │ monitoring. This should happen immediately when the monitored app comes to
 │ the foreground, with minimal visual disruption since MainActivity would
 │ appear briefly before the user returns to their app.
 │ But I need to verify a few things first: what exactly does
 │ `NativeRuleChecker` classify as a "monitored app"? Does it only flag
 │ time-block violations, or does it also recognize apps that should have the
 │ countdown widget? And is there actually a native-side list of monitored apps
 │ I can reference? Let me check how `NativeRuleChecker` is structured to
 │ understand what data I'm working with.

 │ I see that `NativeRuleChecker.checkApp()` gives me what I need—it returns

 │ would be cleaner but requires adding a new Activity and manifest entry.
 │ Looking at this more carefully, the real issue is that the user wants the
 │ countdown widget to appear after the app is killed, which means Flutter
 │ needs to restart and calculate the remaining time. The most pragmatic
 │ solution is to proactively restart MainActivity on the first detection of a
 │ monitored app, using the `FLAG_ACTIVITY_NEW_TASK` flag to launch it without
 │ disrupting the current task stack too much. I'll modify
 │ `MonitorForegroundService.monitorRunnable` step B to check if the app is
 │ monitored but not blocked, and if so, start MainActivity with an action like
 │ "WAKEUP" to trigger the Flutter engine initialization.
 │ To avoid repeatedly restarting MainActivity, I should add a flag in the
 │ service to track whether we've already triggered a wake-up in this cycle,
 │ and reset it when Flutter comes back alive. Then in

 │ action and call `moveTaskToBack(true)` to send it to the background
 │ immediately, so the user stays on their restricted app while Flutter runs in
 │ the background and shows the widget.
 │ Alternatively, I could use a headless Flutter engine that runs without any
 │ UI at all, but that's more complex. The simpler approach is to just start
 │ MainActivity with the WAKEUP action and have it immediately background
 │ itself.

 ▪ 定位到根因：划掉进程后 Flutter 引擎没被重建。原生 MonitorForegroundService
   一直在跑（所以时间块锁能弹），但检测到受监控 app 时不会主动拉起 Flutter
   引擎，导致 Dart 侧的 _showStopwatchWidget 和所有诊断都执行不到。

   修复思路：原生检测到受监控 app 且 Flutter 死亡时，启动 MainActivity
   唤醒引擎，然后立即 moveTaskToBack 把界面藏起来。

 │ allowing the Dart code to display the widget on the next sync check.
 │ There's an expected 5-8 second delay from when the user opens a restricted
 │ app until the widget appears: the first check cycle detects the app, the
 │ engine takes a few seconds to start up, and then the next cycle shows the
 │ widget. Users might also catch a brief flash as MainActivity transitions to
 │ the background, though that should be minimal. I should let them know what
 │ to expect.
 ▪ APK 打好：build/app/outputs/flutter-apk/app-debug.apk

   本次修复原理：
   ┌──────────────┬──────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────┐
   │ 阶段         │ 原行为                   │ 修复后                    │
   ├──────────────┼──────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
   │ 划掉进程     │ Flutter                  │ 同左                      │
   │              │ 引擎死亡，原生服务还在跑 │                           │
   │ 打开受限 app │ 原生检测到但不会唤醒     │ 原生服务以                │
   │              │ Flutter，Dart            │ ACTION_WAKEUP_ENGINE 启动 │
   │              │ 侧代码全部不执行         │ MainActivity 唤醒引擎     │
   │ MainActivity │ —                        │ onStart 检测 WAKEUP       │
   │ 启动         │                          │ action → 立即             │
   │              │                          │ moveTaskToBack 藏到后台   │
   │ Flutter      │ —                        │ 下一轮 _syncAndCheck 执行 │
   │ 引擎恢复     │                          │ _showStopwatchWidget →    │
   │              │                          │ widget 出现               │
   └──────────────┴──────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────┘
   测试步骤：

   1. 安装新 APK（覆盖安装）
   2. 打开 app 一次（确保引擎初始化完成）
   3. 在最近任务中划掉本 app
   4. 打开一个受限 app
   5. 等待约 5-8 秒（引擎启动需要 2-3 秒 + 一轮轮询 5 秒）

   预期：受限 app 上会出现倒计时 widget（或诊断提示框）。可能看到本 app
   界面闪一下就消失（这是 MainActivity 短暂进入前台再 moveTaskToBack
   的正常现象）。

   请测试后告诉我结果：
   - widget 出现了吗？
   - 有无短暂闪屏？
   - 如果还是没出现，是否能看到诊断提示？
